## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (nonlinear oscillators / classical mechanics)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration and the features x, v, t match second-order ODE models of oscillatory motion (x'' = dv_dt) with restoring forces (functions of x), damping (functions of v), and possible external/parametric forcing (functions of t). Nonlinear harmonic oscillator sub-models (Duffing, van der Pol, Mathieu, etc.) are especially plausible.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear (Hookean) oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (small oscillations about equilibrium; sign absorbed in c0)
- Linear damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (viscous damping proportional to velocity)
- Time-forced linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic driving)
- Parametrically excited (Mathieu-type) oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (time-periodic stiffness modulation)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Duffing with forcing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear resonance)
- Quadratic stiffness asymmetry: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (asymmetric restoring force / biased equilibrium)
- Nonlinear damping (quadratic drag-like): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * Abs(v) * v (damping grows with speed)
- van der Pol oscillator (negative linear damping + nonlinear saturation): dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v (self-excited oscillations / limit cycles)
- Rayleigh oscillator (nonlinear damping in v): dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * v**2) * v (self-excitation controlled by velocity-dependent damping)
- Liénard-type general form: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + (c2 + c3 * x**2) * v (broad class of nonlinear oscillators)
- Conservative nonlinear oscillator from potential polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (pure restoring force from U(x) with multiple nonlinear terms)
- State-dependent frequency/curvature: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * x**2) * x + c2 * v (amplitude-dependent stiffness / nonlinear normal modes)
- Mixed coupling nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x * v (damping/restoring coupling; weakly nonlinear expansions)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force structure: dv_dt depending only on x (no v, no t) corresponds to energy-conserving motion with dv_dt = -dU/dx for some potential U(x).
- Hardening vs softening spring: adding +c * x**3 (with sign in c) yields amplitude-dependent frequency; the sign of the cubic term distinguishes hardening from softening behavior.
- Damping identification: terms proportional to v dissipate energy; adding Abs(v)*v or v**3 captures damping that increases strongly with speed and changes decay rates with amplitude.
- Self-excited (limit-cycle) behavior: a damping factor that changes sign with amplitude, e.g., (c0 + c1 * x**2) * v or (c0 + c1 * v**2) * v, produces small-amplitude growth and large-amplitude saturation.
- External forcing signature: additive periodic-in-t terms (sin(c*t), cos(c*t)) indicate driven oscillations and possible resonance/beat phenomena.
- Parametric resonance signature: periodic coefficients multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t)) * x) indicate stiffness modulation and Mathieu-like instability tongues.
- Symmetry cues: odd restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve x -> -x symmetry; even-power terms (x**2) indicate asymmetry/bias or shifted equilibrium.
- Near-equilibrium linearization: if data are small-amplitude, dv_dt often reduces to approximately c0*x + c1*v even when the true system is nonlinear, so higher-order terms should appear only when excursions are large.
- Coupling nonlinearities: x*v or x**2*v terms often arise from truncated expansions of nonlinear damping or coordinate-dependent dissipation; they imply amplitude-dependent damping rates.

- a pure \(\sin(t)\) term (no exponential envelope, frequency 1, phase 0),
- linear \(v\) and cubic \(v^3\),
- an \(x\) term and an \(x\,t\) cross-term (because \(x( a t + 1)= ax t + x\)),
- **no** \(x^3,x^5,x^7\), no constants, no \(v x\), \(v x^2\), logs, abs, etc.

Key necessary conditions for any candidate to match:
1) It must be able to produce an \(x t\) term. None of the candidates include an explicit \(x t\) product; they only have \(x\) times constants/powers of \(x\), plus separate functions of \(t\) (like \(e^{c t}\sin(\cdot)\)) that are **not multiplied by \(x\).** Therefore they cannot generate \(-K\,x\,t\) for all \(x,t\).
2) It must not contain unavoidable extra terms like \(x^5\) with fixed coefficient 1 (many candidates have “+ x**5” with no parameter). Since GT has no \(x^5\), any candidate with a mandatory \(+x^5\) cannot match globally.

With that, evaluate candidates:

1. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 v + c3 + c4 e^{c5 t}\sin(c6 t+c7)+ c8 x^7 + x^5\)  
Has mandatory \(+x^5\) and no \(x t\). Cannot match.

Still mandatory \(x^5\), no \(x t\). Cannot match.

Extra coupling term and no \(x t\). Cannot match.

No \(x t\), mandatory \(x^5\). Cannot match.

5. Has \(c8 x^2\) and mandatory \(x^5\).  
No \(x t\), mandatory \(x^5\). Cannot match.

6. \(c0 x + c1 x^3 + c2 x^5 + c3 v + c4 v^3 + c5 e^{c6 t}\sin(c7 t+c8)\)  
Can set \(c1=c2=0\) to remove \(x^3,x^5\), and tune \(v,v^3\) and sinusoid (set \(c6=0,c7=1,c8=0\)). But still **no \(x t\)** term. Cannot match.

No \(x t\), mandatory \(x^5\). Cannot match.

Even if set \(c1=c2=c4=0\) and tune sinusoid, still no \(x t\). Cannot match.

Trigonometric phase shifts check: many candidates have \(e^{c t}\sin(\omega t+\phi)\). Setting \(c=0,\omega=1,\phi=0\) can match the GT’s \(0.7193\sin t\). This part is not the blocker. The blockers are structural: (i) missing \(x t\) term in every candidate, and (ii) many have unavoidable \(x^5\).

Therefore no candidate can be made identical to the GT for all real \(x,t,v\).

GT Equivalence Verification (PO37)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - c1*beta*v - omega0**c2*(gamma*t + c3)*x
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:** `-0.0856781567252997*v**3 - 1.91960248272986*v - 1.73029531320599*x*(0.0808213006269486*t + 1) + 0.719321236251799*sin(t)`

Let me expand this:
- `-0.0856781567252997*v**3` (v³ term)
- `-1.91960248272986*v` (v term)
- `-1.73029531320599*x*0.0808213006269486*t - 1.73029531320599*x` = `-0.139835...*x*t - 1.73029531320599*x` (x·t term and x term)
- `0.719321236251799*sin(t)` (sin(t) term)

So the GT has these basis functions: **v³, v, x·t, x, sin(t)**

Now, the key question for each candidate is whether it can represent these terms. The critical term is **x·t** — a product of x and t. Let me also note that `sin(t)` needs to be representable. Many candidates use `exp(c*t)*sin(c*t + c)` — if we set the exp coefficient to 0, this becomes `sin(c*t + c)`, which with c=1 and appropriate phase gives `sin(t)`. But we need the x·t cross term.

Let me check: `exp(c5*t)*sin(c6*t + c7)` — setting c5=0 gives `sin(c6*t + c7)`, which can match `sin(t)` with c6=1, c7=0. Good.

**The critical missing piece in most candidates is the x·t term.** None of the candidates I see have an explicit `x*t` term. Let me check if any candidate structure can produce `x*t`:

Looking through all candidates, none have an `x*t` cross-term. The candidates have terms like: x, x², x³, x⁵, x⁷, v, v³, v·x, v·x², sin terms, exp terms, log terms, etc.

**No candidate contains an x·t term.** Since x·t is linearly independent from all other basis functions present (x, x³, x⁵, v, v³, sin(t), etc.), it cannot be constructed from any combination of the available terms.

The only way to get a t-dependent coefficient on x would be through the exp/sin terms, but those don't multiply x. Terms like `exp(c*t)*sin(c*t+c)` are functions of t only, not of x·t.

Therefore, **no candidate can match the GT** because none can produce the `x·t` cross-term that appears in the GT expression `-0.139835...*x*t`.

Let me verify this conclusion by checking each candidate systematically:

Candidates 1-50: All have terms that are either pure functions of x, pure functions of v, pure functions of t (via exp·sin), or cross-terms like v·x, v·x², but **none have x·t**. The x·t term is essential and cannot be zeroed out in the GT (its coefficient is approximately -0.1398, non-zero).
